=500  \\$aMarc-Michel Rey (1720-1780) was a Huguenot printer from Geneva who in 1744 moved to Amsterdam, where he succeeded to Jean-Frédéric Bernard. He was in personal touch with Rousseau. In 1769, Rey issued an 11-volume edition of the "Œuvres de J.-J. Rousseau de Genève. Nouvelle édition revue, corrigée & augmentée de plusieurs morceaux qui n'avoient point encore paru and three volumes of Œuvres diverses". He became the publisher of Voltaire, Rousseau, Diderot, Holbach, etc.

=100  \\$aVerschuere Reijnvaen, Joos$d1737-1808$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q11927169$95830
=245  \\$aMuzijkaal kunst-woordenboek, $bbehelzende de verklaaringen als mede het gebruik en de kracht der kunstwoorden, die in de muzijk voorkomen
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bBrave$c1795
=300  \\$axxii-[ii]-618 pages$b40 plates, musical examples, charts, illustrations
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aJoos Verschuere Reynvaan was a Dutch composer , music writer, organist, carillonneur and doctor of law from the University of Harderwijk. On the cover of one of his works is the title of practicing lawyer (practiserend advocaat). His Musykaal konsworden boeck was the first Dutch work of its kind (Middelburg, 1789), which he did not finish, but later he wrote another work on the same subject, the first part of which it was printed in Amsterdam (1795), but it could not finish this work either. He also composed Cathechismus der Musik (Amsterdam, 1788), in which the author's name appears written Reynwaen. Of his compositions, only three piano sonatas were published.

=100  \\$aRobbers, Jan$d1753-1830$4aut$95234
=245  \\$aTweetal proeven van verhandelingen, over de muzyk, als beeldende kunst, en de muzikale dichtkunde$bIn verband met de compositie van zangmuzyk
=260  \\$aRotterdam$bWijnhoven Hendriksen$c1790
=300  \\$a128 pages$b8 folded pages with musical examples
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aProbably first edition
=500  \\$aJan Robbers was the organist of the Fransche Kerk en Groote Kerk in Rotterdam.
At the age of eighteen, Robbers moved to Rotterdam, where he became bell ringer of the Laurenskerk. In 1778 he was appointed organist of the same church - he held both positions until his death. He also acted as a judge of newly-built organs. His sonatas and sonatinas for harpsichord or piano are a wonderful example of the elegant, light music around 1800.

=500  \\$aThis is the chief work of the Roman historian Lucius Annaeus Florus, who lived at the beginning 2nd century AD. It is an abridgement in four books of Roman history with special reference to the wars waged up to the age of Augustus. It may be considered to be an epitome of Livy, who he sometimes quotes verbatim. Florus also consulted works of Sallust and Caesar. The style is florid and poetic. Florus 'shows a certain literary gift, marred, however,by a strong tendency to rhetoric. His brevity often entails obscurity, though he sometimes produces a felicitous epigram. (.) As an historian he is often inaccurate in both chronology and geography, but the work as a whole achieves a limited success as a rapid sketch of Roman military history'. (OCD, 2nd ed. p. 442)

=500  \\$aThe text takes the form of a verse dialogue between Joseph and Potiphar's wife, derived from the story in the Biblical book of Genesis, focusing on the themes of  Self-control, Love, Virtues and Vices, as part of the Dutch Social life and customs in the 17th century.
=500  \\$aDecorated title page vignet, engraved frontispiece, and two engraved illustrations. Three illustrations are designed by A. van Venne. The first four are signed by their engravers - F. Schillemans, 'TO'?, 'PS' and [illegible]. The title-page vignette and other decorations are unsigned. The first illustration shows Joseph and Potiphar's wife; the second is an allegory (an animal lying within a circle of stones); the third illustration is cut out: it showed a man and woman walking with musicians; the fourth illustration is cut out: it showed a woman being served a meal; the fifth shows a woman with a churn.

=100  \\$aHusen, Heinrich$4aut$95250
=245  \\$aGeheime papieren en bekentenis der Graavin van Lichtenau (vulgo Mientjen Encken)
=260  \\$aCharlottenburg$bs.n.$c1798
=300  \\$a34-36 pages$bengraved and colourored frontispiece 
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aWilhelmine En(c)ke (also called Wilhelmina von Enk, Countess of Lichtenau (1753-1820) also called Countess of Dunkelheim, was the mistress of Frederik Willem II King of Prussia. During her lifetime, she was the subject of satire, and following fake memoirs, she published her own. After the king's death, his son immediately had Wilhelmine investigated for treason and embezzlement, among other things. Although the investigations came to nothing, Lichtenau was taken into fortress custody and banished to Glogau. In 1800, all her assets were confiscated and she received a pension instead. It was not until 1811 that Lichtenau was fully rehabilitated, after she had been partially compensated for her expropriated property in 1809 - at the intervention of Napoleon I - and allowed to return to Berlin.

https://digital.lb-oldenburg.de/vd18/content/titleinfo/623193
and

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aRotgans, Lukas$d1654-1710$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2234173$94983
=245  \\$aBoerekermis
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bHalma$c1708
=300  \\$a67 pages$bpp. 35-38 (one bifolio) are missing$c4°
=500  \\$a"Titelvignet In hoc signo, ongesigneerd, voorts twee fraaie, paginagrote gravures met kermistonelen ... burlesk gedicht in de vorm van een epos over kermisvierende boeren en boerinnen dat tot ver in de negentiende eeuw bijzonder populair was en dan ook vaak is herdrukt. Ook de talrijke navolgingen wijzen op een grote populariteit. Al in het jaar van verschijning werd de 'Boerekermis' met de grootste greetigheit en blakinge, in geen klein getal, begeert en verkocht, schrijft Rotgans' uitgever en vriend François Halma in het voorberecht bij de 'Poëzy' (1715). Volgens Strengholt bestaan er van de eerste uitgave uit 1708 twee drukken: in een niet als zodanig aangemerkte tweede druk is een aantal slordigheden weggewerkt. Buitendien is er in de oudste druk een ‘Zinhinderende Drukfeil’ – in regel 1204 [p. 60], waar boerekleren stond in plaats van boerekroezen – op de laatste bladzij verbeterd. In de tweede editie is die drukfout gecorrigeerd. [Our edition does contain the error, which is corrected in manuscript] ... De in zijn tijd hooggeprezen en veelgelezen Rotgans (Amsterdam 1653 – Breukelen 1710) leidde een ambteloos leven op zijn buitenplaats Kromwijk aan de Vecht bij Breukelen. Behalve dit uitstapje in het boertige genre heeft hij slechts serieuze poëzie geschreven in de daarbij horende parnas-taal, waaronder een echt epos over stadhouder-koning Willem III." (Information taken from https://arinevandersteur.nl/product/boerekermis-quantum-est-in-rebus-inane-amsterdam-samuel-halma-1708/ (5 January 2021):")

=500  \\$aDutch magazine/paper "with geographical, historical, literary, medical, legal, theological, poetic, and oratorical observations, tests, questions, sketches, and treatises" that appeared with irregular frequency between 170 and 1761, and of which several editions were published together in bookform.
=500  \\$acontains "Proefondervindingen over de ademhaling", a letter about medical issues on breathing by Mr. Bremond.
=500  \\$abegins with an 'Interpretation of the Tytel-Prent', (explanation of the title page) in the form of a poem by Pieter Langendijk, followed by the title print on which a facade stone of a Dutch warehouse is revealed (Jan Caspar Philips inv. et fec.).
=500  \\$adedicated to George Clifford (1685-1760) , 'one of the first pillars of the country's renowned commerce; a famous mediator and an excellent promoter of the arts and sciences' Clifford was a Dutch merchant and banker. He is best known as the botanist and zoologist who employed Carl Linnaeus between 1735 and 1738. Clifford was an exponent of the growing public interest in science that developed in the first half of the eighteenth century.

=300  \\$axii-85-[3] pages$bfolded engraved fontispiece 
=500  \\$aDutch magazine/paper "with geographical, historical, literary, medical, legal, theological, poetic, and oratorical observations, tests, questions, sketches, and treatises" that appeared with irregular frequency between 170 and 1761, and of which several editions were published together in bookform. 
=500  \\$abegins with a "Discourse of Severinus Sincerus, held in the Meeting of the Raisonnable Bibliographers, on the 20th of February, 1750, against Philippus Aletophilus, Raised Fellow, and Praesident of the Society of the Raisonnable Bibliographers, and Guardian of the Church. To which are added two letters, as well as an extract from the Acta, and a publication of the highly reputable Society of Biblical Accountants".
The president of this society of wise Bible experts was the Lutheran pastor Philippus Ludovicus Statius Muller (alias Philippus Aletophilus).

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aLa Fargue, Jean Thomas$dc. 1700-1774$4aut$95282
=245  \\$aBeschryvinge van het recht en de gesteltenisse der Barrière
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bDe Cros$c1746
=300  \\$a[iv]-172 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aLa Fargue was a French poet, notary, and orangist pamphletist. Being a fleeing Huguenot he settled in the Netherlands and married Charlotte Constantia van Nieuwland (1703 -1785). 
=500  \\$aThe treatise of Barriere was declared in 1709 in The Hague and 1715 in Antwerp, whereby the Dutch Republic v. Germany and England was granted the right to erect a barrier in the Eastern Netherlands against France by laying siege to a number of towns (barrier towns). In 1781 the barrier towns were evacuated by the Republic on request of Emperor Joseph II. The only time that the barrier towns had to serve against France, during the War of the Austrian Succession, they turned out to be completely useless because the fortifications were neglected and the occupation was insufficient (1744).

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aVaucanson, Jacques de$d1709-1782$4aut$95299
=245  \\$aLe Mécanisme du flûteur automate
=260  \\$aParis$bGuerin$c1738
=300  \\$a20 pages$bmodern paper cover, side sewn binding
=500  \\$aFrontispiece is missing
=500  \\$amanuscript note on title page "de lacademie des (? ...)  originaire de Grenoble . Valler h"
=500  \\$aIn 1737, Vaucanson built The Flute Player, a life-size figure of a shepherd that played the tabor and the pipe and had a repertoire of twelve songs. The figure's fingers were not pliable enough to play the flute correctly, so Vaucanson had to glove the creation in skin. The following year, in early 1738, he presented his creation to the Académie des Sciences.Johann Joachim Quantz, court musician and long-time flute instructor to Frederick II of Prussia, discussed the shortcomings of Vaucanson's mechanical flute player. In particular its inability to sufficiently move the lips resulted in the necessity of increasing the wind pressure for the upper octaves. Quantz discouraged this method as producing a shrill, unpleasant tone.

=300  \\$a[i]-13 pages$bpaper bound, engraved title page
=500  \\$aVery little is known about Vincenzo Panerai (c. 1750-c. 1790) other than that he studied composition alongside Luigi Cherubini in Florence. Cherubini is known to have praised the performance of Panerai's music in that city in the 1770s. A teacher and author of several didactic works, Panerai published one of the few fingering tables for flute that survives from Italy during his lifetime.

He also published a Chorale Book, dedicated to the church warden of the reformed churches of Rotterdam.

=100  \\$aGillet$cCitoyen$4aut$95324
=245  \\$aÉcole de Terpsichore,$bou Principes raisonnés de la musique vocale
=260  \\$as.l.$cc. 1790
=300  \\$a168 pages
=500  \\$a"Le C[itoy]en Gillet", hence around the French Revolution
=500  \\$a"Zeer bijzonder manuscript!!" (according to Ton Koopman)
=500  \\$aInserted letter from Anik Devriès to Luc Van Dijck (Muziekcentrum van de Omroep, the previous owner?), Paris, 7 September 1990, mentioning the fruitless search for Gillet's identity
=500  \\$aInserted note by Eline Holl, who has also looked for further information about the author, without results: a presumed author, Alexander Gillet (1749-1826), was a preacher and composer active in the USA
=500  \\$aThis ms., featuring numerous calligraphical elements, looks as though having been prepared for print
=500  \\$aThe author writes in the 'avant-propos': "Ce n'est point la manie d'être auteur qui m'a fait composer ce traité mais bien le désir de donner moi-même à mes enfants les elemens de la musique, et ce d'essayer d'un moyen qui pût plûtôt que tout autre connu ou usité jusqu'alors de leur en faciliter l'étude. Dans cette intention j'ai tenté de traiter les principes de cette science d'une manière à amener mes enfants, par un langage ordinaire et qui leur fut familiariser à la connaissance des mots techniques de cet art, et par là, leur en faire sentir toute la signification ce que j'ai crû nécessaire avant que de leur en faire faire l'application. Le succès a couronné mon attente, au point qu'avant deux mois de leçon de deux heures par jour, mes deux enfants chantaient en partie avec moi avec la justesse de sons et la précision de mesure qui fait l'ame de la musique [...]"
=500  \\$aPaper in roughly the first half shows a watermark of a fleur-de-lis within an escutcheon topped by crown combined with a countermark “P ROUSSEL”. Paper in the second half shows a plain fleur-de-lis combined with a single-letter countermark (illegible because only partially visible in the gutter)

=563  \\$a19th-c. red cloth binding with red leather spine, blind-embossed boards and blind- and gold-embossed decoration of the spine. Author (“Le c.en Gillet”) and title gold-tooled on the spine. Shell-pattern marbled endpapers and a single additional free endleaf both front and rear

=500  \\$aFrançois Halma (1653-1722) was a Dutch printer, publisher and bookseller, successively in Utrecht, Amsterdam and Leeuwarden. Halma published many works, in the fields of theology, philosophy and geography, among others.
=590  \\$aComposé sur le modèle des dictionaires de Richelet, Pomey, Tachard, et Danet. Revû & considérablement augmenté sur le Dictionaire & le Grammaire de l’Académie françoise. On y a adjouté un excellent Traitté de l'Orthographe de la langue françoise. Dat is, Het groot Fransch en Nederduitsch woordenboek, opgestelt naar het voorbeeldt der woordenboeken van Richelet, Pomey, Tachard, en Danet. Overzien, en merkelyk vermeerdert op het woordenboek en de spraakkunst van het Koningklyk Genootschap, eerst ontworpen door C. Rouxel en F. Halma. Vervolgens naaukeurig overzien, en met alle bovengemelde woordenboeken en andere vergeleken: ook met ontelbaare woorden en spreekwyzen verrykt en naar de gronden der beste Nederduitsche schryveren beschaaft, verbetert, herstelt, en in orde gebragt door François Halma. Hier is bygevoegt een uitmuntend werkje over de spellinge der Fransche taale

=100  \\$aRameau, Jean-Philippe$d1683-1764$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1145$94787
=245  \\$aCode de musique pratique,$bou Méthodes pour apprendre la musique, meme à des aveugles, pour former la voix & l'oreille
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bImprimerie Royale$c1760
=300  \\$axx-185 pages$bengraved frontispiece
=500  \\$a"Rameau's last published book on harmonic theory. Working with the fundamental principles of harmonic theory established in his revolutionary 'Traité de l'Harmonie' (1722), Rameau presented in the 'Code' an alternative explanation for the derivation of the minor third (based on the upper partials of a vibrating body). He also classified the suspension as a type of substitution, and "attempted to relate proportion in music to that in other disciplines, [seeking] to confirm the derivation of music from a universal, cosmic principle founded on nature and on unity" (GDM). This last theoretical flight of fancy, which Rameau had stated before in his 'Observations sur notre instinct pour la musique' (1756), was the major cause of Rameau's break with the Encyclopedists. The controversy is detailed in Rameau's 'Origine des Sciences' and 'Lettre à M. D'Alembert,' both bound in with this copy of the 'Code'." (from an inserted note printed on paper from John Howell - Books San Francisco)

=500  \\$aAs a fundamental work in the development of Western music, it earned Rameau the reputation of being one of the most accomplished musicians of his time.The Treatise describes music and how to write it based on the tonal system used today. =001  587
=008  220518s1726\\\\|||afg||\||||\00|\0\fre\d
=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aRameau, Jean-Philippe$d1683-1764$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1145$94787
=245  \\$aNouveau système de musique théorique
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bBallard$c1726
=300  \\$aviii-114-[6] pages$b2 folded sheets inserted
=500  \\$aThe' Nouveau système de musique théorique' is the second treatise on music theory written by Jean-Philippe Rameau. With this work, he completed his 'Traité de l'harmonie réduite à ses principes naturel's of 1722, and presented it as an introduction to the latter.

In the meantime, he had become aware of Joseph Sauveur's work on the harmonic resonance of the sound body, which corroborated, in terms of physics and auditory perception, the principles set out in his first book. The perception of harmonics (or consonances) when the fundamental sound is emitted had already been noted by the Jesuit scholar Marin Mersenne.

Whereas the entire theoretical approach in the previous treatise was based exclusively on mathematical considerations, in his Nouveau système Rameau refers to the physical phenomenon of harmonic sounds that are, so to speak, 'consubstantial' with the fundamental sound. Their inevitable presence is the basis of Nature and, for the author, justifies the notion of perfect harmony.

=100  \\$aRameau, Jean-Philippe$d1683-1764$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1145$94787
=245  \\$aDémonstration du principe de l'harmonie :$bservant de base à tout l'art musical théorique et pratique
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bDurand$bPissot$c1750
=300  \\$axlvii-112-[4] pages$b5 folded sheets inserted
=500  \\$a"Though Rameau had already stated the fundamental principles of his revolutionary theory of harmony in his 'Traité de l'harmonie' of 1722, he continued to revise and adapt the new system until his death some forty years later. In 'Demonstration', Rameau offered a new derivation of the minor third (based upon a theory of multiple generation), and "altered his view of the subdominant [recognizing] its position as a product of musical experience rather than of nature" (GDM). Rameau submitted 'Demonstration' to the Academie Royale des Sciences, which gave the work its approval." (from an inserted note printed on paper from John Howell - Books San Francisco)

=100  \\$aStanley, John$d1712-1786$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q726286$94965
=240  \\$aop. 5, op. 6 & op. 7
=245  \\$aTen Voluntaries for the Organ or Harpsichord
=260  \\$aLondon$bHarrison & Co$cs.d.
=300  \\$a28-24-27 pages
=500  \\$aCharles John Stanley (1712-1786) was an English composer, violinist and organist. He had an accident when he was 2, which left him almost blind. Despite that, Stanley had a remarkable memory, which helped him direct many of Handel's oratorios and to enjoy music-making and card games with friends. If he had to accompany a new oratorio he would ask his sister-in-law to play it through just once – enough to commit it to memory. He frequently played the organ at the Vauxhall Gardens and was first choice to play at charity events and at the launch of any newly built church organs. He even found time to teach. His oratorio Jephthah was first performed in 1757. 
=500  \\$aExists in various modern editions; every opus nr. contains 10 voluntaries
=500  \\$aSee also 03J49
=501  \\$aBound in with Händel's 'Six Fugues or Voluntary's'
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1748 (opus 5), 1752 (opus 6) & 1754 (opus 7)

=100  1\$aClément, Charles François$d1719-1799$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q34933718$95347
=245  \\$aJournal de clavecin composé sur les ariettes de comédies, intermèdes et opéras comiques, qui ont eu le plus de succès
=260  \\$aParis$bClément$c1769
=300  \\$a72 pages
=500  \\$aCharles-François Clément (1719-1799) was a harpsichord teacher in Paris. Besides the Journal, he adapted several Italian operas for Parisian audiences, notably Niccolò Jommelli's 'L'Uccelatrice', which he renamed 'La Pipée', and Rinaldo di Capua's 'La Zingara', renamed 'La Bohémienne'. These two works were staged in 1766. Among his original works are a series of pieces for violin and harpsichord and three songs '(Le départ des guerriers' & 'Le retour des guerriers' in 1750 and 'Le Célibat' in 1762). He also wrote two theoretical books, 'Essai sur l'accompagnement du clavecin' (1758) and' Essai sur la basse fondamentale' (1762).
=500  \\$aJanuary-December 1769 issues of this periodical, which ran from 1762 to 1772

=500  \\$aJohn Garth (1721-1810) was an English composer, musician and teacher. Garth is chiefly remembered for his eight-volume edition with English text of The First Fifty Psalms Set to Music by Benedetto Marcello (1757–65). He also composed a set of cello concertos (op. 1, 1760) and five sets of harpsichord sonatas (opp. 2, 4–7, 1768–82), among other works.

=300  \\$a[i]-64 pages
=500  \\$aGeorge Guest (1771-1831) was an English organist and composer. He was chorister of the Chapels Royal, and may have been the "Master Guest" who was one of the principal singers (in Messiah and miscellaneous concerts) for the Hereford musical festival of 1783. Guest was organist at Eye, Suffolk, in 1787, and at St. Peter's, Wisbech, Cambridgeshire, from 1789 to 1831.

=260  \\$aLeipzig$bBreitkopf & Härtel$c1824 [?]
=300  \\$a25 pages
=500  \\$aAugust Wilhelm Bach (1796-1869) was a German composer and organist. He is unrelated to the family of Johann Sebastian Bach. In 1816 he served as an organist at St Mary's Church and from 1820 he taught organ and music theory at the Institute of Church Music set up by Zelter. In 1832, Bach succeeded Zelter as the director of the Royal Institute of Church Music in Berlin. He also taught at the Prussian Academy of Arts. His compositions largely consist of sacred works and works for keyboard. He also wrote a pipe organ method and a hymnbook.

=100  \\$aPasquali, Nicolò$d1718-1757$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q4346510$95368
=245  \\$aThorough-Bass Made Easy
=260  \\$aLondon$bBremner$c1765
=300  \\$a29 pages
=500  \\$aPasquali, Niccolò, Italian violinist and composer (c.1718-1757). He travelled to Edinburgh (1740), London (c. 1743 & 1750-52) and Dublin (1748–49 & 1751-52) but in the end settled in Edinburgh, where he published the valuable treatise 'Thorough-bass made easy' (1757) and 'The Art of Fingering the Harpsichord' (Edinburgh, 1758). Besides that, his oeuvre includes 12 overtures (London, 1751), 6 sonatas for Violin and Basso Continuo (1744), 2 sets of 3 sonatas for 2 Violins, Viola, and Basso Continuo (1750), many minuets, and numerous songs.
=500  \\$aBremner was a Scottish publisher who in 1754 set up a printing company in Edinburgh (see 05D09 and 09K25) which moved to London around 1762
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1757

=041  \\$aeng
=059  \\$aorg/hpd
=100  \\$aStanley, John$d1712-1786$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q726286$94965
=240  \\$aop. 5, op. 6 & op. 7
=245  \\$aTen Voluntaries for the Organ or Harpsichord
=260  \\$aLondon$bThompson$cs.d.
=300  \\$a38-32-33 pages
=500  \\$aCharles John Stanley (1712-1786) was an English composer, violinist and organist. He had an accident when he was 2, which left him almost blind. Despite that, Stanley had a remarkable memory, which helped him direct many of Handel's oratorios and to enjoy music-making and card games with friends. If he had to accompany a new oratorio he would ask his sister-in-law to play it through just once – enough to commit it to memory. He frequently played the organ at the Vauxhall Gardens and was first choice to play at charity events and at the launch of any newly built church organs. He even found time to teach. His oratorio Jephthah was first performed in 1757. 
=500  \\$aExists in various modern editions; every opus nr. contains 10 voluntaries
=500  \\$aSee also 03J15b
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1748 (opus 5), 1752 (opus 6) & 1754 (opus 7)

=245  \\$aNun danket alle Gott! Concertstück für die Orgel
=260  \\$as.l.$bKörner$c1846-65
=300  \\$a13 pages
=500  \\$aWilhelm Valentin Volckmar (1812-1887) was a German organ virtuoso, music teacher and composer.
=500  \\$aIn 1835 he became a seminary music teacher in Homberg (Efze) in North Hesse. He became famous as an organ virtuoso, and in 1846 he was appointed Dr. h.c. and in 1886 professor. During his lifetime, Volckmar was famous as an organist, especially because of his masterful pedal playing, but also as an improviser and theoretician. He maintained friendly relations with Franz Liszt, who also arranged for a papal asucription. Because of his numerous instrumental pedagogical works, he was also called the also called the "Czerny" of the organ.

=008  210309s1811\\\\be\g|||||||||\00|\0\fre\d
=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aZimmermann, Pierre Joseph-Guillaume$d1785-1853$4trc$95391
=245  \\$aCours de composition par Louis Cherubini commencé le 3 février 1811
=260  \\$as.l.$c1811
=300  \\$a137 pages
=520  \\$aCourse notes of lessons with Luigi Cherubini (1760-1842), commenced 3 February 1811. Apart from three pages, the manuscript is entirely in Zimmermann's autograph. The work is divided into seven books and more or less follows the published version of Cherubini's 'Cours de contrepoint et fugue' as printed later in 1835, albeit in an abridged version and with numerous differences to the text and musical examples. One of the most significant aspects of the manuscript is the date in Zimmermann's hand: "commencé le 3 février 1811". It is known that in the first two decades of the nineteenth century Cherubini compiled many didactic works at various intervals for the use of students. Until now his 'Cours de contrepoint et fugue' (in collaboration with Halévy) was thought to have been a much later work. The connections between Cherubini, Halévy and Zimmermann are close: Zimmermann became a pupil of Cherubini at the Paris Conservatoire around 1805, taught there himself from 1811 and was appointed professor of counterpoint and fugue in 1821, though he declined the position and taught piano only. In 1811 Halévy became a pupil of Cherubini's and may have well been taught by Zimmermann. The manuscript itself embodies some of Cherubini's earliest theoretical ideas, doubtless copied by Zimmermann from the author's original. On its publication, over twenty years later, the 'Cours de contrepoint et fugue' became one of the most popular and widely used didactic works in nineteenth-century Europe (notes by Lisa Cox, Antiquarian).
=533  \\$aDigitized by iGuana, Spring 2022

=500  \\$aBorn and died in Salisbury, Joseph Corfe (1741-1820) spent much of his life at the cathedral as a chorister, and as organist (1792 - 1804). In 1783 he was appointed a Gentleman of the Chapel Royal and sang in the Handel commemmoration in the following year. He published a volume of church music comprising a service and eleven anthems, three sets of glees, and this Treatise on Thorough Bass which was used well into the nineteenth century.

=100  1\$aPollini, Francesco$d1762-1846$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1351579$95394
=245  \\$aMetodo pel clavicembalo
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aMilan$bRicordi$c1811
=300  \\$a84 pages$bmusic examples
=500  \\$aFrancesco Giuseppe Pollini (1762-1846) was an Italian pianist, composer and academic. He moved to Vienna in 1783, and was a student there of Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart. He returned to his birthplace Ljubljana, performing there as a singer and actor. In Italy he appeared as a pianist, violinist and opera singer, appearing in several cities. From 1790 he lived mainly as a piano teacher in Milan, where in 1793 he took lessons from Niccolò Antonio Zingarelli. From 1809 he was a professor of piano at Milan Conservatory. Pollini was highly regarded by his contemporaries; Vincenzo Bellini dedicated the opera La sonnambula to him.

=041  \\$aeng
=100  \\$aHawkins, John$d1719-1789$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q661076$95399
=245  \\$aA General History of the Science and Practice of Music
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aLondon$bPayne$c1776
=300  \\$a5 vols. (lxxxiv-465+544+535+548+482-[58] pages)$bengraved frontispiece, illustrations, music examples
=500  \\$aA late 19th-century edition of this work is also available in the library
=520  \\$aSir John Hawkins (1719-1789) was an English magistrate, writer, and author of the first history of music in English. Hawkins was apprenticed as a clerk and became a solicitor. In 1759 a legacy enabled him to sell his practice. A Middlesex magistrate from 1761, Hawkins was elected chairman of the quarter sessions in 1765. He was knighted in 1772. Hawkins's General History of the Science and Practice of Music occupied him for sixteen years. It was published in five volumes in 1776, a few weeks before Charles Burney's celebrated General History of Music. Hawkins's book continues to be invaluable as a mine of detailed information, some of it unavailable elsewhere, but it was eclipsed by Burney's.

=100  \\$aSpieß, Meinrad$d1683-1761$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1918163$95409
=240  \\$aop. 8
=245  \\$aTractatus musicus compositorio-practicus
=260  \\$aAugsburg$bLotter$c1746
=300  \\$a[ix]-220-[4]-11 pages$bengraved frontispiece, title page in red and black ink, music examples
=500  \\$aMeinrad Spieß, actually Matthäus Spieß (1683-1761) was a German Benedictine monk and composer.
=500  \\$aRISM B VI, 2, S. 802
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1745
=561  \\$aEx libris "Imp. Monrii Neresheim" (manuscript) & M. L. H. C. (plate)
=590  \\$adas ist, Musicalischer Tractat, in welchem alle gute und sichere Fundamenta zur Musicalischen Composition aus denen alt- und neuesten besten Autoribus herausgezogen, zusammen getragen, gegen einander gehalten, erkläret, und mit untersetzten Exemplen dermassen klar und deutlich erläutert werden, daß ein zur Musique geartetes, und der edlen Musicalischen Composition begieriges Subjectum oder angehender Componist alles zur Praxin gehöriges finden, leichtlich, und ohne mündliche Instruction begreiffen, erlernen und selbst mit volkommenem Vergnügen zur würklichen Ausübung schreiten könne, und därffe. Samt einem Anhang In welchem fast alle, sowohl in diesem Werck, als auch in andern Musicalischen Schrifften in Griechisch- Lateinisch- Welsch- Frantzösisch- und Teutscher Sprach gebräuchliche Kunst- und andere gewöhnlich- vorkommende Wörter nach Ordnung des Alphabets gesetzt, und erkläret werden. Herausgegeben von R. P. Meinrado Spiess, Des ohnmittelbahren Freyen Reichs-Stüffts, und Gotteshauses U. L. F. in Yrrsee O. S. P. Benedicti Profess, Capitularn, und Sub-Priorn, Auch der Löbl. correspondirenden Societaet Musicalischer Wissenschafften in Teutschland Mitglied. Opus VIII.

=100  \\$aSorge, Georg Andreas$d1703-1778$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q88592$97274
=245  \\$aAusführliche und deutliche Anweisung zur Rational-Rechnung,$bund der damit verknüpften Ausmessung und Abtheilung des Monochords
=260  \\$aBad Lobenstein$bSorge$c1749
=300  \\$a[viii]-308-[4] pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$a Sorge's membership in Lorenz Christoph Mizler's Correspondierender Societät der musicalischen Wissenschaften, to which he was admitted in 1747 as the fifteenth member after Johann Sebastian Bach, led to a number of disputes. The first of these was a dispute over a new tonal system introduced by Georg Philipp Telemann.
The initial cause was a dispute over a new tonal system of dividing the octave into 55 microintervals introduced by Georg Philipp Telemann. Since Telemann had only formulated the general conditions of his system, the Society, which was very involved in mathematical questions, insisted on receiving the exact mathematical calculation from the author. Since Telemann was unwilling to do so and was obviously neither aware of nor interested in such calculations, Sorge presented these mathematical definitions of Telemann's system in his writings after a dispute with the Societät member Christoph Gottlieb Schröter.

=500  \\$aJohan Adam Remmers was organist of the Amsterdam Mennonite Church 'near the Lamb' from 1777 to 1780, thereafter of the Waalse Church in Amsterdam (thus still in 1793, and after 1806). His organ accompaniments to the Mennonite hymns of 1793 suggest that he was then organist of another Mennonite church (perhaps 'De Zon,' because the hymns are those of this congregation).

=059  \\$aorg
=100  \\$aSamber, Johann Baptist$d1654-1717$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q38263774$95455
=245  \\$aContinuatio ad manuductionem organicam.$bDas ist: Fortsetzung zu der Manuduction oder Hand-Leitung zum Orgl-Schlagen
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aSalzburg$bMayr$c1707
=300  \\$a[viii]-95 pages$b15 plates, oblong, musical examples
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Elucidatio musicæ choralis'
=520  \\$aThe personality and work of the Austrian cathedral organist from the archdiocese of Salzburg, music theorist and court musician Johann Baptist Samber, have so far been little researched. His writings offer information on performance practice, organ music or organ building, basso continuo, counterpoint, musical rhetoric and solmisation. Samber, who describes himself as a pupil of Andreas Hofer and Georg Muffat, wrote three important works on composition: the 'Manuductio ad organum' (1704; see 04C06c), a 'Hand-Leitung zum Orgl-Schlagen', its sequel, the present 'Continuatio ad manuductionem organicam' (1707), and the 'Elucidatio musicæ choralis' (1710; this convolute). It is characteristic of the first two works that Samber's instrumental and compositional instruction is based almost exclusively on the basso continuo and the traditional voice leading rules. Significant are his careful and detailed descriptions and remarks on German fugue compositions of the late 17th century.

=100  \\$aSamber, Johann Baptist$d1654-1717$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q38263774$95455
=245  \\$aManuductio ad organum.$bDas ist: Gründlich- und sichere Handleitung, Durch die höchst-nothwendige Solmisation zu der Edlen Schlag-Kunst.
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aSalzburg$bMayr$c1704
=300  \\$a[xvi]-177-[6] pages$b42 Plates, musical examples, oblong
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe personality and work of the Austrian cathedral organist from the archdiocese of Salzburg, music theorist and court musician Johann Baptist Samber, have so far been little researched. His writings offer information on performance practice, organ music or organ building, basso continuo, counterpoint, musical rhetoric and solmisation. 
=500  \\$aSamber, who describes himself as a pupil of Andreas Hofer and Georg Muffat, wrote three important works on composition: 
the "Manuductio ad organum" (1704), a "Hand-Leitung zum Orgl-Schlagen", 
its sequel, the "Continuatio ad manuductionem organicam" (1707)
and the "Elucidatio musicae choralis" (1710).
It is characteristic of the first two works that Samber's instrumental and compositional instruction is based almost exclusively on the basso continuo and the traditional voice leading rules. Significant are his careful and detailed descriptions and remarks on German fugue compositions of the late 17th century.
Samber's third work, the "Elucidatio musicae choralis", teaches the basics for the performance of Gregorian chant. This choral teaching is aimed primarily at the next generation of clerics and aspiring organists and "regentes chori".

=500  \\$a"Continuatio ad Maniductionem organicam" see 04C06a
=504  \\$afacsimile reprint  Olms, Hildesheim, 2009. ISBN 978-3-487-14267-8 
=561  \\$aEx Libris Alfred Cortot (Plate) and Sambure (information provided by TK)
=590  \\$aDenen Anfangenden zu sondern Nutz und Ergoetzung, einigen Lehrmeistern aber zu Anleitung und Behueff, die Jugent mit geringer Muehe in guter Ordnung nach Anweisung dess zu End-gesetzten Registers zu instruiren. Sambt einer kurtz-verfassten Information von denen Kirchen- oder Choral-Tonen, wie solche geschwind zu erkennen, und auff denen in Cornet-Ton gestimmen Orgl-Wercken abzuschlagen seynd. Alles mit vilen in Kupffer gestochenen Figuren und Exemplen gezieret, und mit sonderbahren Fleiss zusammen getragen, auch das erste Mahl in den Druck gegeben

=059  \\$av bc
=100  \\$aAgostini, Serafino$4asn$920916
=245  \\$a... ad uso di Serafino Agostini
=260  \\$aFlorence$c17xx
=300  \\$a168 pages
=500  \\$aContains 12 cantatas for soprano and bc
=500  \\$aThe first cantata, an early version of Händel's soprano cantata 'Tu fedel? Tu costante?', was recorded by Ton Koopman for Antoine Marchand/Challenge Classics, in 2016. The cantata was noticed by Eline Holl and authenticated by the American musicologist John Roberts. Probably composed in Venice in 1706, near the start of Handel’s Italian sojourn, the ‘new’ cantata initially follows the course of the familiar version, HWV171 (with oboe added to the strings), then goes its own way. While the text, a woman’s taunting of her rustic Fileno, is the same, the music of this newly discovered version is more wistful, even sorrowful in cast, epitomised by the plangent siciliano aria ‘Se Licori, Filli ed io’.
=500  \\$aAccording to John Roberts, 'Tu fedel? tu costante?: Two Versions of Handel Cantata', Händel-Jahrbuch 64 (2018), 335-366: 337, the manuscript was probably already bound at the time it was copied in Florence and long before Serafino Agostini acquired it. Handel probably composed this cantata in Venice, in keeping with Benedetto Marcello's cantatas.
=505  \\$aTu fedel, tu costante (HWV 171a) / Handel -- Aure soavi, e liete (HWV 84) / Handel -- Più che porto / Marcello -- In di selve e prati / Marcello -- Or de' miei lunghi / Marcello -- Onda d'amaro pianto / Marcello -- Cori che amando andate / Marcello -- Mi costa sante lacrime / Marcello -- Occhi del viver mio dolci sostegni (two versions) / Marcello -- Varia pur dolce Amor / Marcello -- Deh volate all'idol mio / Marcello
=533  \\$aDigitized by iGuana, Spring 2022. A facsimile of 'Tu fedel? tu costante?' (HWV 171a) was edited by John H. Roberts for the Hallische Händel-Ausgabe, V:5a (Kassel: Bärenreiter, 2016).

=041  \\$ager
=059  \\$ahpd
=100  \\$aNeupert, Hanns$d1902-1980$4aut$95478
=245  \\$aDas Cembalo:$bEine geschichtliche und technische Betrachtung der Kielinstrumente
=260  \\$aNuremberg$bNeupert$c1935
=300  \\$a24 pages$bloose leaflets
=500  \\$aAdvertisement booklet by the J.C. Neupert company
=500  \\$aContains loose leaflets advertising listing national critics on Neuperts cembalo models; as wel as early music editions by Peters
=520  \\$aHans Neupert studied technical physics and musicology in Munich and Erlangen. Subsequently practical training in piano making. In 1928 he joins the piano factory in Bamberg founded by his grandfather Johann Christoph Neupert, which has also been making new harpsichords since 1907, later also clavichords,  keel instruments and fortepianos, so that the company soon achieves a leading position on the German market. In accordance with this specialisation, the company is renamed 'Workshops for Historical Keyboard Instruments'. In 1968 he bequeathed the collection of historical instruments founded by his grandfather to the Germanisches Nationalmuseum in Nuremberg. Numerous publications on the history of the piano, including 'Vom Musikstab zum modernen Klavier' (1925, 4th ed. 1960), 'Das Cembalo' (1933, 4th ed. 1966) and 'Das Klavichord' (1942, 2nd ed. 1956).

=041  \\$aeng
=100  \\$aBusby, Thomas$d1754-1838$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7788082$95213
=245  \\$aConcert Room and Orchestra Anecdotes of Music and Musicians, Ancient and Modern
=260  \\$aLondon$bClementi$c1825
=300  \\$a3 vols. (xvi-304+x-288+x-302 pages)$efold-out plates
=500  \\$aBrief anecdotes on various composers and performers, mostly compiled from external sources, as the author acknowledges in the preface, p. iv: "The articles now presented to the public, have, in many instances, been collected from sources that lay far out of common reach ..." However, as he argues at p. v: "many of the narratives and anecdotes in these volumes are the results of a reminiscence founded on the professional practice and personal connection of three score years, and have never met the public eye." The book in fact contains many descriptions of recently-invented instruments and theaters, interesting biographies of English musicians, insights on aesthetics, etc.
=500  \\$aThe title-page of vol. 1 depicts the façade of the Italian Opera House in London, with a fold-out reproducing the setup of the Handel Commemoration in Westminster Abbey (see 03K12). Vol. 1 furthermore contains engraved portraits of Carl Maria von Weber, Elizabeth Billington and Joseph Haydn, as well as facsimiles of musical fragments by the Earl of Kelly, Arnold, Arne and Croft (also included in vol. 3), and a fold-out indicating the compass of voices and instruments. The title-page of vol. 2 depicts Benjamin Flight & Joseph Robson's Apollonicon (described in vol. 1, pp. 3-4) and the façade of the Argyle Rooms, and furthermore contains portraits of Charles Burney and Henry Purcell, as well as a fold-out with a facsimile of the musical handwriting of Henry Purcell, Samuel Wesley and Johann Sebastian Bach. Vol. 3 has a title-page depicting the façade of the London Odeon, portraits of Jean-Baptiste Lully, Thomas Augustine Arne and John Braham, and a fold-out representing the musical handwriting of Pleyel, Boyce, Dibdin, Tartini, Shield and Haydn.

=100  \\$aMarnix van St. Aldegonde, Philips van$d1538-1598$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q701605$95502
=245  \\$aDe Bijencorf der H. Roomsche Kercke
=260  \\$aUtrecht$bBilsteyn$c1648
=300  \\$a[xiv]-[468]-[12] pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aPhilips van Marnix, lord of Sint-Aldegonde (1540-1598) was a writer, diplomat, intellectual and consultant to William of Oranje. He may have authored the Wilhelmus.
=500  \\$a'De Byencorf der H. Roomsche Kercke' was in its time one of the most famous written combats against the Roman Catholic Church. The author does this in the form of a defense: he pretends to give an explanation of a work of a French Catholic known at that time, who calls on the Calvinists to rejoin the Mother Church. Marnix pretends to offer a positive addition to that booklet, but under that mask the Calvinist is speaking. Holy indignation alternates with coarse mockery that the contemporary could enjoy, just as he also accepted the verbose nature of the booklet without any objection. Supporters and opponents have devoured this booklet, as the reprints and the many writings about it show.
=500  \\$aDescriptive ms. notes in the back
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1569
=590  \\$aBy den Auteur Vergroot ende Vermeerdeert

=500  \\$aDavid Lindelbach was the director of the Amsterdam Schouwburg in 1687-88
=500  \\$aBetween 1685 and 1687, Lingelbach was involved in setting up an opera in Buiksloot, outside the town's jurisdiction. After one season, the project proved unfeasible for repetition. In 1687, he was appointed director of Van Campen's theatre, alongside Jan Pluimer. Because of the bad economic times, a violent stock market crash in which Coenraad van Beuningen lost half a million guilders, preparations for the invasion by Stadholder William III and the looming Nine Years' War, visitors stayed away.

=100  \\$aAlbrechtsberger, Johann Georg$d1736-1809$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q314164$95150
=245  \\$aSämmtliche Schriften über Generalbaß, Harmonie-Lehre, und Tonsetzkunst:$bzum Selbstunterrichte
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aVienna$bHaslinger$c1837
=300  \\$a3 vols. (xvi-208+[ii]-273-[6]+[vi]-208 pages)$bmusical examples
=520  \\$aJohann Georg Albrechtsberger (1736-1809) was an Austrian composer and organist who enjoyed a wide reputation as music theorist, teaching Ludwig van Beethoven, Ignaz von Seyfried, Johann Nepomuk Hummel, Ignaz Moscheles, Anton Reicha, Franz Xaver Wolfgang Mozart, and Josef Weigl. In 1792, he became Kapellmeister of St. Stephen's Cathedral instead of Mozart, who had passed away. Possibly the most valuable service he rendered to music was in his theoretical works. In 1790 he published at Leipzig a treatise on composition, of which a third edition appeared in 1821. An English version of this was published by Novello in 1855. His compositional style derives from the counterpoint of Johann Joseph Fux, who was Kapellmeister at St Stephen's Cathedral from 1713 to 1741. Ignaz von Seyfried (1776-1841), who edited Albrechtsberger's works, was also a keyboard student of Mozart.
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1826, see 08A15, H.02.070, and H.02.071
=561  \\$aH.02.032: Ex libris Carlo Ferdinand Bischof (stamp)
=590  \\$aSystematisch geordnet, mit zahlreichen, aus dessen mündlichen Mittheilungen geschöpften Erläuterungs-Beyspielen, und einer kurzen Anleitung zum Partitur-Spiel, nebst Beschreibung alles bist jetzt gebräuchlichen Instrumente. Mit 556 Notenbeispielen.

=500  \\$aMichel-Paul Guy de Chabanon (Saint-Domingue, 1730-10 June 1792, Paris) was a violinist, composer, music theorist, and connoisseur of French literature. He was elected to the Académie des inscriptions et belles-lettres (1760) and the Académie française (1779). His double identity as a writer and a musician gave him a unique viewpoint on the links between music and language and in developing a philosophy of music of which his work was the expression. He also contributed to defining opera as a musical genre.

=059  \\$av
=100  \\$aBérard, Jean-Antoine$d1710-1772$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1684590$95483
=245  \\$aL'Art du chant
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bDessaint; Saillant; Prault; Lambert$c1755
=300  \\$a[xvi]-158-[6]-34 pages$bmusical examples
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$adedicated to Madame de Pompadour, the official chief mistress of King Louis XV from 1745 to 1751, who remained influential as court favourite until her death
=500  \\$aincludes an anatomical plate of the lungs
=500  \\$aAuthorship claimed by the Abbé Blanchet, who afterward published his "L'art, ou les principes philosophiques du chant" (Paris, 1756) as "2. édition, corrigée & augmentée." a designation that arises from the publication in 1755 of L’art du chant, dedié a Madame de Pompadour by Jean-Antoine Bérard, whom Blanchet accuses of incorporating his material. The two works certainly include many passages which are almost identical, notably the first and third chapters, ‘La voix considérée par rapport au chant’ and ‘La formation de la voix’. Blanchet in turn seems to have based much of his work upon the physician and anatomist Antoine Ferrein’s De la formation de la voix de l’homme (1741), although he refutes this imputation.
Joseph Blanchet was not a musician but a priest and, in his own words, ‘homme de lettres amateur’.

=500  \\$aconcludes with a 34-page appendix containing vocal airs by Rameau, Campra and others.

=500  \\$aThe translator, Pietro Denis, also known as Pierre Denis, was an Italian mandolin virtuoso and teacher, and composer, who studied under Giuliano in Naples and established himself in Paris. 
=500  \\$aCited in Koopman 1985, pages 21, 79-82 ("zeer lezenswaardig")

=534  \\$aItalian original text originally published in 1752-56, with French text first published in 1770
=590  \\$aContenant l'origine de la petite note, sa valeur, la manière de la placer, toutes les différentes espèces de cadences, la manière de les employer, le tremblement et le mordant, l'usage qu'on en peut faire, les modes ou agrémens naturels, les modes artificiels qui vont à l'infini, la manière de former un point d'orgue. Ouvrage original non seulement aux maitres de goût du chant, mais encore à tous les joueurs d'instrumens, et que tout bon musicien même compositeur lira avec beaucoup de plaisir.

=100  \\$aSorge, Georg Andreas$d1703-1778$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q88592$97274
=245  \\$aCompendium harmonicum,$boder Kurzer Begriff der Lehre von der Harmonie, vor diejenigen welche den Generalbaß und die Composition studiren, in der Ordnung welche die Natur des Klangs an die Hand giebt
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aBad Lobenstein$bSorge$c1760
=300  \\$a[xiv]-121-[3]-[24] pages$bmusic examples
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aSorge was an organist, composer, and, most notably, theorist. His references to Johann Sebastian Bach show that they were friends, and he composed three fugues for organ on the name BACH (BWV Anh. 107, 108 and 110). He joined Lorenz Christoph Mizler's Corresponding Society of Musical Sciences in 1747, just a month after Bach himself.
=500  \\$aSorge's writings on thorough-bass and harmony are very competent, and his theoretical grasp of unequal temperaments excelled even that of J. G. Neidhardt (though still taking 1⁄12 comma as an indivisible unit of measure. He cited Bach as 'witness' that regular 1⁄6-comma meantone temperament was inadequate to 'modern' harmony, and he dismissed Johann Philipp Kirnberger's schemes of temperament as 'no good'.[Wikipedia]

=100  \\$aPrelleur, Peter$d1705-1741$4aut$95540
=245  \\$aThe Modern Musick-Master or, The Universal Musician …
=260  \\$aLondon$bPrelleur$c1731
=300  \\$a[xii]-48-[iv]-48-[iv]-48-[iii]-48-[iv]-48-[iv]-48-[i]-20-4 pages$b6 folded pages, musical noatation, 6 engraved frontispieces
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aContains: "An Introduction to Singing"
=500  \\$a"Directions for Playing on the Flute"
=500  \\$a"The Newest Method for Learners on the German Flute"
=500  \\$a"Instructions upon the Hautboy"

=500  \\$a"The Harpsichord Illustrated and Improv'd"
=500  \\$a"A Brief History of Musick, and a Musical Dictionary"
=500  \\$aContains 8 beautiful frontispieces, engraved by I.Smith, appropriate to each part, most depicting people playing musical instruments.
=500  \\$awith 7 folding plates of instruction, fingering charts, and musical examples
=500  \\$amainly musical notation, less text
=500  \\$aPeter Prelleur was of French extraction and in early life a writing master. About 1728 he was elected organist of St. Alban, Wood Street, and shortly afterwards engaged to play the harpsichord at Goodman's Fields Theatre, which he continued to do until the suppression of the theatre under the Licensing Act in 1 737, composing also the dances and occasional music. In 1730 he published « The Modern Musick Master, or, the Universal Musician/ containing an introduction to singing, instructions for playing the flute, German flute, hautboy, violin, and harpsichord, with a brief History of Music, and a Musical Dictionary ». In 1735 he was elected the first organist of Christ Church, Spitalfields. After the closing of Goodman's Fields Theatre he was engaged at a newly opened place of entertainment in Leman Street close by, called the New Wells, for which he composed some songs, and an interlude entitled « Baucis and Philemon », containing a good overture and some pleasing songs and duets, the score of which he published. Fifteen hymn tunes by him were included in a collection of twenty-four published by one Moze, an organist, in 1758, under the title of « Divine Melody », in which he is spoken of as if then dead. 
=504  \\$aindex
=590  \\$aContaining I An Introduction to Singing ... II Directions for Playing on the Flute ... III The Newest Method for Learners on the German Flute ... IV Instructions upon the Hautboy ... V The Art of Playing on the Violin... VI The Harpsichord Illustrated and Improv'd ... A Large collection of Airs and Lessons ... With a brief history of Musick ... to which is added a musical dictionary.
